Refuting the Three Properties of Continuous Quantity
The author enumerates and refutes three properties used to argue for continuous quantity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the three alleged properties of continuous quantity—difference, division, and enumeration—are explained on the atomist hypothesis without positing a continuous quantity.

Core Idea
The three properties of bodies do not prove continuous quantity; atoms explain them all.

In this passage, the author addresses the philosophers' argument that certain observable features of bodies—like differences in size, divisibility, and being countable—require a continuous quantity (al-miqdar). He shows that each of these features can be accounted for on the atomist model of discrete parts. This refutation is central to the kalam defense of atomism against the Aristotelian notion of continuous magnitude.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage carefully, then the English translation. Notice the three properties (التفاوت, القسمة, العد) and how the author handles each.
The passage is dense; don't worry about every detail on first read.
2
Identify the three refutations
For each property, note the author's counter-argument. Difference in size is due to number of atoms; division is hypothetical separation of atoms; enumeration is by counting atoms directly.
The third property includes an important nuance about illusion (الوهم).
3
Understand the role of illusion
The author acknowledges that we might imagine a continuous unit when counting, but he dismisses this as an illusion arising from our senses' inability to perceive tiny separations.
This shows the author's commitment to atomism even against common perception.
4
Connect to the overall argument
Reflect on how all three refutations together undermine the philosophers' case for continuous quantity. The body can have these features solely through its atomic composition.
This lesson is a direct application of the atomist framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثاني - المقصد السادس : إنهم أنكروا المقدار. الإشارة إلى الخواص الثلاثة المذكورة للكمية، وأنها كيف تتصور في الجسم على تقدير تركبه من الجواهر الأفراد فقال: ( والتفاوت ) بين الأجسام في الصغر والكبر والزيادة والنقصان ( راجع إلى قلة الأجزاء وكثرتها فما هو أقل أجزاء يكون أصغر حجماً وأنقص، وقد يقع التفاوت بسبب شدة اتصال الأجزاء وثبوت فرج فيما بينها، فقد جاز أن يوصف الجسم بالمساواة واللامساواة من غير أن تقوم به كمية اتصالية تسمى مقداراً ( والقسمة ) الفرضية العارضة للجسم على ذلك التقدير (معناها فرض جوهر دون جوهر ) فإن كل واحد منهما شيء مغاير للآخر فقد صح على الجسم ورود القسمة بدون كمية اتصالية قائمة به ( ولا عاد له غير الأجزاء ) أي يجوز أن الجسم بكل واحد من الجواهر الفردة التي هي أجزاؤه وليس هناك شيء آخر يعد به ان حجم الجسم متصل واحد أصلاً ( اللهم إلا بالوهم) فإنه قد يتوهم ويفرض فيه بعض من ذلك المتصل بحيث يعده فيتخيل أن هناك مقدارا هو كم متصل يمكن أن يفرض فيه واحد عاد ( وحكمه مردود ) لأنه نشأ من عدم الإحساس بالمفاصل والانفصال لعجز الحس عن إدراك تفاصيل الأمور الصغيرة جدا فقد العد في الجسم بلا كمية اتصالية وبما ذكرناه انكشف أنه لا يمكن الاستدلال بثبوت شيء من هذه الأمور الثلاثة في الجسم على وجود مقدار قائم به
The second observation - the sixth purpose: They denied quantity. Reference to the three properties mentioned for quantity, and how they are conceived in the body on the assumption that it is composed of individual atoms. He said: (Difference) between bodies in smallness and greatness, increase and decrease (goes back to the fewness and multiplicity of parts, so what has fewer parts is smaller in volume and less, and difference may occur due to the intensity of connection of parts and the existence of gaps between them. So it is permissible for the body to be described as equality and inequality without there being a continuous quantity called 'magnitude' (miqdar). And (division) the hypothetical division that occurs to the body on that estimation (its meaning is the supposition of one atom without another) for each of them is something different from the other, so it is valid for the body to undergo division without a continuous quantity subsisting in it. (And it has no enumerator other than the parts) meaning it is permissible that the body is each of the individual atoms that are its parts, and there is no other thing by which it is enumerated, that the size of the body is a single continuum at all (except by illusion) for one may imagine and suppose in it some of that continuum such that he enumerates it, and he imagines that there is a magnitude that is a continuous quantity in which a unit can be supposed (and its judgment is rejected) because it arises from the lack of sensation of joints and separation due to the incapacity of sense to perceive the details of very small things. So enumeration occurs in the body without a continuous quantity. And by what we have mentioned, it is revealed that it is not possible to infer, by the existence of any of these three things in the body, the existence of a magnitude subsisting in it.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage refutes the philosophers' claim that three observable properties of bodies—difference in size, divisibility, and having an enumerator—prove the existence of a continuous quantity (al-miqdar). The author shows that these properties are explainable on the atomist hypothesis without positing a continuous quantity. First, difference in size is due to the number of atoms (fewer atoms = smaller body). Second, hypothetical division means supposing one part separated from another, which does not require a continuous quantity; atoms are distinct. Third, having an enumerator (count) is just the parts themselves; any imagined continuous unit is an illusion due to our senses' inability to perceive minute separations. Thus none of the three entail a continuous quantity.

Misconception: If a body can be divided hypothetically, it must have a continuous quantity that is being divided.
Correction: Division can be understood as the mental separation of discrete parts (atoms) without any continuous substance between them.

Checkpoint

A) The amount of continuous quantity in each body
B) The number of parts (atoms) in each body
C) The intensity of connection between parts
D) The shape of the body

Key Takeaway
The three properties of bodies can all be explained by the number and arrangement of discrete atoms, without needing a continuous quantity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that the ability to count parts of a body does not prove a continuous magnitude; the counting is of discrete atoms. Is there a belief you hold about your own inner self—that it is a continuous, unified 'I'—that might actually be composed of discrete moments or parts? How would you know the difference, and what would change if you broke it down?
?
The author says the illusion of continuous quantity arises because the senses cannot perceive gaps. In your daily life, where might you be assuming continuity—in your thoughts, your intentions, your worship—that is actually fragmented? Will you examine one such area today and look for the hidden 'gaps'?
?
If the physical world is truly atomistic and not continuous, what does that imply about the metaphysical principles you rely on? Are you willing to let go of intuitive assumptions about continuity in favor of what reasoning and revelation indicate?

Potential and Actual Quantity: Defending Against an Objection
Al-Jurjani responds to an objection using potential vs actual distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why quantity can change in actuality while remaining the same in potentiality, and why this does not undermine the proof that quantity is superadded to substance.

Core Idea
Quantity can be one potentially but many actually—showing it is not the particles.

Al-Jurjani addresses an objection that quantity does not change when shapes differ because the area remains the same. He distinguishes between potential and actual quantity to show that actual quantities do differ while the substance remains, supporting the view that quantity is an additional attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the first part of the passage where the opponent claims quantity is unchanged because the area is the same. Understand their reasoning.
The objection relies on the idea that the product of dimensions is constant.
2
Identify the distinction
Notice how Al-Jurjani responds by distinguishing between potential (bi al-quwwa) and actual (bi al-fi'l) quantity. The area is one potentially, but actual quantities differ with shape.
This distinction is key to refuting the objection.
3
Reflect on significance
Ask yourself: Why does this distinction show quantity is not identical to the parts? Because the parts (substance) do not change, while the actual quantity changes with shape.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثاني - المقصد السادس : إنهم أنكروا المقدار
يقال : لا يتغير المقدار فيما ذكرتم من المثال بل يختلف الأشكال واختلافه لا يستلزم اختلاف المقدار ( إذ المساحة واحدة ) في جميع هذه الصور المتبدلة ( لأنا نقول المساحة واحدة بالقوة أي مضروب أحدهما كمضروب الآخر، وأما بالفعل فالاختلاف في المقدار (ظاهر) لأن ذلك الجسم له مع التدوير كمية مخصوصة في الجهات ومع التكعيب كمية أخرى ممتدة فيها على وجه آخر فالمقادير المتواردة مختلفة بالفعل وإن كانت متحدة بالقوة من حيث أن المساحة الحاصلة منها بطريق الضرب واحدة وهذا الاتحاد لا يقدح في إثبات ما هو المطلوب ( وأيضاً فالماءان إذا اتصلا فقط بطل السطح المتعدد ( الذي كان لهما وحدث سطح آخر هو واحد ( والشيء ) الواحد كالماء في كوز ( إذا قطع ( بأن صب مثلا في كوزين زال عنه سطحه الواحد و ( حصل فيه سطحان بعد العدم وكل ذلك الذي ذكرناه من زوال مقدار جسمي إلى مقدار آخر ومن زوال سطحين وحدوث سطح واحد، ومن زوال سطح واحد وحدوث سطحين ( يعطي الوجود أي وجود المقدار الذي هو الجسم التعليمي والسطح لأن الزائل والمتجدد المذكورين ليسا محض العدم بل هما موجودان زال أحدهما وحدث الآخر (و) يعطي ( التبدل) أي توارد المقادير الجسمية والسطحية على سبيل البدل ( وبه ) أي بهذا التبدل ( تبين أنه ) أعني المقدار (لا يكون نفس الأجزاء بل أمراً زائداً لأنها حاصلة في الحالتين غير متبدلة بخلاف الجسم التعليمي والسطح، ولما ثبت السطح مع كونه متناهياً في الوضع ثبت الخط الذي هو طرفة كما أنه إذا ثبت تناهي الجسم فقد ثبت السطح أيضا
The second observation - the sixth section: They denied the quantity. It is said: The quantity does not change in the example you mentioned, rather the shapes differ and their difference does not necessitate the difference of quantity (since the area is one) in all these changing forms. (We say: The area is one in potentiality, i.e., the product of one is like the product of the other. But in actuality, the difference in quantity is apparent because that body, when rounded, has a specific quantity in directions, and when cubed, has another quantity extended in it in another way. So the successive quantities are different in actuality even if they are one in potentiality in that the area obtained from them by multiplication is one, and this unity does not harm proving what is sought. (Also, if two waters connect, the multiple surface they had vanishes and another single surface occurs.) And the one thing, like water in a jug, if it is divided (e.g., poured into two jugs), its single surface disappears and two surfaces occur after non-existence. All that we have mentioned—from the cessation of a bodily quantity and the occurrence of another quantity, from the cessation of two surfaces and the occurrence of one surface, and from the cessation of one surface and the occurrence of two surfaces—indicates existence, i.e., the existence of the quantity which is the mathematical body and surface, because the ceased and renewed things mentioned are not pure non-existence, but they are existing; one ceased and the other occurred. And it indicates change, i.e., the succession of bodily and surface quantities alternatively. And by this change, it becomes clear that it, i.e., the quantity, is not the same as the parts but an additional matter because they (the parts) exist in both states, unchanging, unlike the mathematical body and surface. And since the surface is established while being finite in position, the line which is its extremity is established, just as when the finitude of the body is established, the surface is also established.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a proof that quantity (al-mikdar) is an attribute superadded to the substance and not identical to the parts. The argument begins by stating an objection: it is claimed that quantity does not change when the shape changes, because the area remains the same. The response distinguishes between potential and actual quantity. Potentially, the area product remains constant; but actually, the quantity differs because the body's dimensions vary with shape. Then a further proof is given using water: when two bodies of water join, their separate surfaces disappear and a single new surface appears; when one body is divided, one surface vanishes and two surfaces appear. These changes demonstrate that surfaces (a type of quantity) come into and out of existence, proving they are not the same as the underlying substance (the water particles), which remain unchanged. The conclusion is that quantity is an additional attribute, not identical to the particles. Finally, the finitude of surfaces in position entails the existence of lines, just as finitude of bodies entails surfaces, reinforcing the reality of these quantities.

Key Terms
المقدار
المساحة
بالقوة
بالفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Jurjani's response, why does the constancy of the area not prove that quantity is unchanged?
A) Because the area is actually different in each shape
B) Because the area is only potentially one, while actual quantities differ
C) Because the particles change when the shape changes
D) Because the objection is based on a false premise

Key Takeaway
Quantity is not identical to substance; it can be one potentially but many actually, as shown by the distinction between potential and actual quantity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever mistaken something that is only potentially true for an actual reality, like assuming that because a situation has the same 'area' (outward factors) it must be the same in essence? Where in your life are you mixing potential and actual, and what change is required of you to see things as they truly are?
?
Al-Jurjani shows that the same substance can have different actual quantities depending on its arrangement. How often do you judge people or situations by a single measurement (like their outward appearance or a single action) while missing the different 'actual quantities' of their character? Will you commit to looking beyond the superficial 'area' to discern the inner reality?
?
The opponent clung to the sameness of area to deny change. Is there an area of your faith where you are clinging to a 'potential unity' to avoid recognizing a needed actual change? What excuse are you using to resist transformation that Allah calls you to?

Water Examples: Quantity Changes While Substance Remains
Al-Jurjani uses water examples to prove quantity is superadded, then extends to lines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the examples of water joining and separating demonstrate that surfaces (a type of quantity) come into and out of existence while the substance remains, proving quantity is an additional attribute.

Core Idea
When water joins, surfaces merge; when it splits, surfaces multiply—but the water stays the same.

Al-Jurjani uses concrete examples of water to demonstrate that surfaces come into and out of existence while the underlying substance remains unchanged. This shows that quantity is an attribute superadded to the particles, not the particles themselves. He then extends the argument to show that lines are also established through the finitude of surfaces.

Guided Path
1
Read the water examples
Read the passage describing two waters connecting and one water dividing. Visualize the changes in surfaces.
Notice that the water particles themselves do not change, only the surfaces.
2
Understand the conclusion
Al-Jurjani concludes that the change in surfaces indicates that quantity is not the same as the parts because the parts persist.
Think about why the persistence of substance is key.
3
Reflect on the extension to lines
The last sentence connects the finitude of surfaces to the existence of lines. This reinforces the reality of mathematical objects.
This is a further implication of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثاني - المقصد السادس : إنهم أنكروا المقدار
يقال : لا يتغير المقدار فيما ذكرتم من المثال بل يختلف الأشكال واختلافه لا يستلزم اختلاف المقدار ( إذ المساحة واحدة ) في جميع هذه الصور المتبدلة ( لأنا نقول المساحة واحدة بالقوة أي مضروب أحدهما كمضروب الآخر، وأما بالفعل فالاختلاف في المقدار (ظاهر) لأن ذلك الجسم له مع التدوير كمية مخصوصة في الجهات ومع التكعيب كمية أخرى ممتدة فيها على وجه آخر فالمقادير المتواردة مختلفة بالفعل وإن كانت متحدة بالقوة من حيث أن المساحة الحاصلة منها بطريق الضرب واحدة وهذا الاتحاد لا يقدح في إثبات ما هو المطلوب ( وأيضاً فالماءان إذا اتصلا فقط بطل السطح المتعدد ( الذي كان لهما وحدث سطح آخر هو واحد ( والشيء ) الواحد كالماء في كوز ( إذا قطع ( بأن صب مثلا في كوزين زال عنه سطحه الواحد و ( حصل فيه سطحان بعد العدم وكل ذلك الذي ذكرناه من زوال مقدار جسمي إلى مقدار آخر ومن زوال سطحين وحدوث سطح واحد، ومن زوال سطح واحد وحدوث سطحين ( يعطي الوجود أي وجود المقدار الذي هو الجسم التعليمي والسطح لأن الزائل والمتجدد المذكورين ليسا محض العدم بل هما موجودان زال أحدهما وحدث الآخر (و) يعطي ( التبدل) أي توارد المقادير الجسمية والسطحية على سبيل البدل ( وبه ) أي بهذا التبدل ( تبين أنه ) أعني المقدار (لا يكون نفس الأجزاء بل أمراً زائداً لأنها حاصلة في الحالتين غير متبدلة بخلاف الجسم التعليمي والسطح، ولما ثبت السطح مع كونه متناهياً في الوضع ثبت الخط الذي هو طرفة كما أنه إذا ثبت تناهي الجسم فقد ثبت السطح أيضا
The second observation - the sixth section: They denied the quantity. It is said: The quantity does not change in the example you mentioned, rather the shapes differ and their difference does not necessitate the difference of quantity (since the area is one) in all these changing forms. (We say: The area is one in potentiality, i.e., the product of one is like the product of the other. But in actuality, the difference in quantity is apparent because that body, when rounded, has a specific quantity in directions, and when cubed, has another quantity extended in it in another way. So the successive quantities are different in actuality even if they are one in potentiality in that the area obtained from them by multiplication is one, and this unity does not harm proving what is sought. (Also, if two waters connect, the multiple surface they had vanishes and another single surface occurs.) And the one thing, like water in a jug, if it is divided (e.g., poured into two jugs), its single surface disappears and two surfaces occur after non-existence. All that we have mentioned—from the cessation of a bodily quantity and the occurrence of another quantity, from the cessation of two surfaces and the occurrence of one surface, and from the cessation of one surface and the occurrence of two surfaces—indicates existence, i.e., the existence of the quantity which is the mathematical body and surface, because the ceased and renewed things mentioned are not pure non-existence, but they are existing; one ceased and the other occurred. And it indicates change, i.e., the succession of bodily and surface quantities alternatively. And by this change, it becomes clear that it, i.e., the quantity, is not the same as the parts but an additional matter because they (the parts) exist in both states, unchanging, unlike the mathematical body and surface. And since the surface is established while being finite in position, the line which is its extremity is established, just as when the finitude of the body is established, the surface is also established.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a proof that quantity (al-mikdar) is an attribute superadded to the substance and not identical to the parts. The argument begins by stating an objection: it is claimed that quantity does not change when the shape changes, because the area remains the same. The response distinguishes between potential and actual quantity. Potentially, the area product remains constant; but actually, the quantity differs because the body's dimensions vary with shape. Then a further proof is given using water: when two bodies of water join, their separate surfaces disappear and a single new surface appears; when one body is divided, one surface vanishes and two surfaces appear. These changes demonstrate that surfaces (a type of quantity) come into and out of existence, proving they are not the same as the underlying substance (the water particles), which remain unchanged. The conclusion is that quantity is an additional attribute, not identical to the particles. Finally, the finitude of surfaces in position entails the existence of lines, just as finitude of bodies entails surfaces, reinforcing the reality of these quantities.

الجسم التعليمي
السطح
الخط
التبدل

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that quantity is identical to the substance because it seems inseparable from the body.
Correction: The water examples show that surfaces can appear and disappear while the water particles remain, proving quantity is a separate attribute.

Checkpoint

A) That quantity is identical to the water particles
B) That a single surface can become two surfaces without the water changing
C) That water has no real quantity
D) That surface is not a real attribute

Key Takeaway
The water examples demonstrate that quantity (surface) changes independently of the substance, proving it is an additional attribute, not identical to the parts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Are you defined by your changing surface or by your unchanging soul? How will you remind yourself daily that your worth is not in your physical form?
?
When you look at a glass of water, do you see only the water or do you acknowledge the reality of its surface as a distinct creation of Allah? How does recognizing that every accident is created separately deepen your appreciation of Allah's power and wisdom?
?
The example shows that what seems to be a single surface can become two without altering the water. In your relationships, do you sometimes mistake changing external forms (like words or actions) for a change in the underlying essence? How can this lesson help you forgive others when their 'surface' changes while their essence remains?

Second Proof: Genuine Rarefaction
Al-Jurjani argues from genuine dilatation to prove quantity as an additional attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Jurjani uses genuine rarefaction to argue for the existence of quantity as an additional attribute, and the distinction between genuine and metaphorical rarefaction.

Core Idea
Genuine rarefaction proves that quantity is a real attribute, not just particle rearrangement.

In this passage, al-Jurjani presents his second proof for the existence of quantity, focusing on the phenomenon of genuine rarefaction. He argues that when a body expands without adding matter or creating voids, the increase in volume can only be explained by the presence of a distinct quantity attribute. He also carefully distinguishes this genuine process from metaphorical rarefaction, which involves the mere entry or exit of parts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the core argument
Locate the main proof: a body can increase in volume without adding parts or creating a vacuum. Ask yourself why this implies quantity is an attribute.
3
Examine the distinctions
Notice the distinction between genuine and metaphorical rarefaction, and the discussion of finitude in position versus quantity. Reflect on how these clarify the proof.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثاني الجسم يتخلخل تخلخلاً حقيقياً، وهو أن يزداد حجمه من غير انضمام شيء آخر إليه ومن غير أن يقع بين أجزائه خلاء كالماء إذا سخن تسخيناً
قوله: (مع كونه متناهياً في الوضع أي في الإشارة الحسية إشارة إلى أنه لو لم يكن متناهياً في الوضع كسطح الكرة لا يستلزم وجود الخط . قوله : (تناهي الجسم أي في الوضع والمقدار بناء على أن تناهيه في المقدار الثابت تناهي الأبعاد يستلزم تناهيه في الوضع. قوله : ( تخلخلاً حقيقياً ) احتراز عن انتفاش الأجزاء واند ماجها فإنه يسمى تخلخلاً وتكائفاً مجازياً، فإنه ليس إلا دخولاً أجزاء خارجية عن الجسم وخروجها . قوله: (مع كونه متناهياً في الوضع التناهي على قسمين: تناء في الوضع وهو كون المقدار بحيث يشار إلى طرفه إشارة حسية وتناه في المقدار وهو كونه بحيث يمكن أن يفرض مقدار محدود بقدره ثم السطح إنما يستلزم الخط إذا تناهى في الوضع وأما إذا لم يتناه فيه كما في محيط الكرة الغير المتناهي فيه، وإن وجب تناهيه في المقدار بالبرهان الدال على تناهي إبعاد الجسم مطلقاً فلا ولهذا قال : مع كونه متناهياً في الوضع وكذا الكلام في استلزام الخط للنقطة إذ لا نقطة في محيط الدائرة فالسطح ليس بمستلزم للخط ولا الخط للنقطة ، وأما الجسم فيستلزم للسطح عندهم لوجوب تناهيه في المقدار المستلزم لتناهيه في الوضع كما يشهد به التخيل الصحيح ولذا أطلق استلزام تناهي الجسم للسطح. قوله : فلا يثبت على رأيه وجود مقدار (أصلاً أما الجسم التعليمي والسطح فلما ذكر صريحاً وأما الخط فلانه نهاية السطح فإذا لم يثبت وجوده لم يثبت وجوده للوجه الذي ذكر فيها
The second point: The body undergoes genuine rarefaction, i.e., its volume increases without the addition of anything else to it and without a void occurring between its parts, like water when heated strongly. His saying: 'while being finite in position' means in sensory indication, indicating that if it were not finite in position like the surface of a sphere, it would not entail the existence of a line. His saying: 'the finitude of the body' means in position and quantity, based on the fact that its finitude in fixed quantity (finitude of dimensions) entails its finitude in position. His saying: 'genuine rarefaction' is a precaution against the swelling (intifash) of parts and their coalescence (indimaj), for that is called metaphorical rarefaction and condensation, for it is nothing but the entry of external parts into the body and their exit. His saying: 'while being finite in position' – finitude is of two types: finitude in position, which is that the quantity is such that its extremity is pointed to by sensory indication, and finitude in quantity, which is that it is possible to posit a limited quantity equal to it. Then the surface only entails the line if it is finite in position, but if it is not finite in it, as in the circumference of an infinite sphere [which is not actually infinite, but hypothetically], and if its finitude in quantity is necessary by the proof showing the finitude of the dimensions of the body absolutely, then no [line is entailed]. Therefore he said: 'while being finite in position'. Likewise, the entailment of a line for a point [is not automatic], for there is no point on the circumference of a circle. So the surface does not entail the line, nor does the line entail the point. But the body entails the surface according to them because of the necessity of its finitude in quantity, which entails its finitude in position, as sound imagination witnesses. Hence, they [the theologians] assert unconditionally that the finitude of the body entails the surface. His saying: 'So, according to his view, no existence of quantity is established at all' – as for the mathematical body and surface, it is clear from what was mentioned; as for the line, because it is the end of the surface, if its existence is not established, then its existence is not established for the reason mentioned therein.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage presents the second argument for the existence of quantity as an additional attribute: genuine rarefaction (al-takhalukh al-haqiqi). The main proof states that a body can increase in volume without adding external matter or creating a vacuum, as when water is heated. This volume increase cannot be explained by particle rearrangement alone; it implies the existence of a quantity attribute that can change. The commentary clarifies terms: 'genuine rarefaction' excludes metaphorical rarefaction, which is merely the entry or exit of parts. It also explains that the finitude of surfaces in position entails lines, but only if the surface is finite in position (unlike a sphere's surface, which is finite in magnitude but not in position). The commentary further notes that the body's finitude in quantity necessarily entails finitude in position, which then entails surfaces. The final note reiterates that on the atomist view, no quantity exists at all, including bodies, surfaces, and lines.

التخلخل الحقيقي
التخلخل المجازي
الانتفاش
الاندماج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All volume increase is due to particles entering or leaving the body.
Correction: Genuine rarefaction shows volume can increase without particle addition, implying a distinct quantity attribute.

Checkpoint
What distinguishes genuine rarefaction from metaphorical rarefaction according to the commentary?
A) Genuine rarefaction involves a vacuum
B) Metaphorical rarefaction is only the entry or exit of parts
C) Genuine rarefaction requires added matter
D) There is no difference

Key Takeaway
The phenomenon of genuine rarefaction demonstrates that quantity is an additional attribute beyond the particles themselves.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience a genuine increase in your Iman or spiritual understanding, do you tend to attribute it to external factors (like a good lecture or company) rather than recognizing it as a real, inward expansion of your soul granted by Allah? This lesson insists that genuine rarefaction is a real change from within, not just added particles. Are you willing to see your spiritual growth as a true, divinely-given transformation—or do you reduce it to mere accumulation of knowledge or deeds?
?
The passage warns against confusing metaphorical rarefaction (apparent change) with genuine rarefaction (actual increase in reality). In your life, are there areas where you mistake surface-level adjustments for genuine, interior change—for instance, in your character, your prayers, or your repentance? Will you ask Allah to show you the difference and to grant you the genuine transformation of the heart that only He can produce?
?
Al-Jurjani's proof shows that denying quantity as a real attribute leads to denying the reality of surfaces, lines, and points altogether. Could it be that denying the deeper spiritual realities (like the soul, accountability, or divine providence) leads you to a worldview where nothing truly substantial remains? What would it cost you to accept that there are real, intangible attributes to your existence that cannot be reduced to physical processes?

Refutation of the Argument for Magnitude from the Atomist Perspective
Al-Isfahani refutes the argument for magnitude by showing it presupposes atomism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Isfahani refutes the argument for magnitude by revealing its dependence on the denial of atomism and how the atomist explains apparent change through the rearrangement of indivisible parts.

Core Idea
Magnitude arguments fail against atomism because atomists explain change as part rearrangement, not new existence.

In this passage, al-Isfahani tackles a key argument for the existence of magnitude—that bodies and surfaces have inherent size. He shows that this argument only works if one rejects atomism. For the atomist, what seems like change in magnitude is merely the transfer and repositioning of indivisible parts, not the creation or annihilation of anything.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the structure: first a statement, then the atomist's two replies.
The passage is a single continuous argument.
2
Identify the main claim
Find where al-Isfahani states that proving magnitude depends on denying the indivisible part. Highlight this conditional relationship.
This is the key refutation strategy.
3
Understand the atomist's explanation for magnitude change
The atomist says that what appears as different magnitudes is actually parts moving from length to width or vice versa. No new magnitude arises.
The atomist denies genuine change, only rearrangement.
4
Examine the atomist's explanation for surface
The atomist explains surfaces simply as connection or separation of parts, not as a distinct magnitude.
This extends the same logic to two-dimensional magnitudes.
5
Reflect on the broader significance
Consider why this refutation matters in kalam: it shows that arguments for magnitude are not universally valid but depend on specific metaphysical commitments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عما ذكر في إثبات المقدار الجسمي والسطحي أنه فرع نفي الجزء الذي لا يتجزأ وأما من قال به وبتركب الجسم منه فإنه لا يسلم حدوث شيء لم يكن وعدم شيء بل يقول فيما ذكرتم من توارد المقادير المختلفة على جسم واحد ما كان من الأجزاء في الطول انتقل إلى العرض وبالعكس فليس هناك توارد مقادير مختلفة بل انتقال الأجزاء من جهة إلى جهة وتبدل أوضاعها وبذلك يختلف أشكال الجسم، ويقول فيما ذكرتم في إثبات السطح ليس هناك إلا اتصال أجزاء جسم بأجزاء جسم آخر أو انفصال أجزاء جسم واحد بعضها عن بعض فلا يثبت على رأيه وجود مقدار أصلاً.
And the answer to what was mentioned in proving bodily magnitude and surface magnitude is that it is a branch of the denial of the indivisible part. But as for the one who affirms it and the composition of the body from it, he does not concede the occurrence of something that was not and the non-existence of something. Rather, he says concerning what you mentioned of the succession of different magnitudes on a single body: what was of the parts in length moved to width and vice versa, so there is no succession of different magnitudes, but rather a transfer of parts from one direction to another and a change of their positions, and by that the shapes of the body differ. And he says concerning what you mentioned in proving the surface: there is nothing there except the connection of the parts of a body with the parts of another body or the separation of the parts of one body from each other. So, according to his opinion, the existence of any magnitude is not established.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the argument for the existence of bodily magnitude (al-miqdar al-jismi) and surface magnitude (al-miqdar al-sathi) from the perspective of the atomist who affirms the indivisible part (al-juz' alladhi la yatajaza). The passage begins by stating that the argument for magnitude is a branch of the denial of the indivisible part, meaning it only works if one rejects atomism. For the atomist, the body is composed of indivisible parts, and what appears as change in magnitude is actually just rearrangement of those parts. The author explains that the atomist does not accept that something new comes into existence or something ceases to exist. Rather, when different magnitudes seem to succeed each other on the same body, the atomist says that the parts have merely shifted from length to width or vice versa, so there is no succession of different magnitudes, only transfer and change of positions. Similarly, when a surface appears, the atomist says it is just the connection or separation of parts. Therefore, according to atomism, the existence of any magnitude (whether bodily, surface, or line) is not established; it is only apparent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the atomist denies all forms of magnitude entirely, meaning nothing has size or extension.
Correction: The atomist does not deny apparent magnitude; he explains it as the rearrangement of indivisible parts. There is no real change in magnitude, but there is observable extension resulting from part positions.

Checkpoint
According to the atomist, what explains the appearance of different magnitudes on the same body?
A) The body's essence changes.
B) The parts of the body move and change positions.
C) The body acquires new parts from outside.
D) The body loses parts.

Key Takeaway
The atomist does not accept real change in magnitude; apparent change is due to rearrangement of parts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see changes in your health, wealth, or relationships, do you immediately assume something has been 'created' or 'destroyed'? What if these changes are simply Allah rearranging atoms in a way that you cannot fully perceive? How does this perspective affect your gratitude or patience?
?
You have just learned that atomism explains apparent differences in shape and size by the transfer of parts. In your own life, when you compare yourself to others, you may see differences in capability or circumstance. Could it be that Allah has simply arranged the same 'parts' (your potential, your experiences) differently for each person? How does this thought challenge your envy or pride?
?
The passage says 'there is no succession of different magnitudes, but rather a transfer of parts'. Today, when you experience a sudden change—good or bad—will you attribute it to a new creation or to a reconfiguration of what already existed? How can remembering that Allah is the Re-arranger strengthen your reliance on Him?

Proof of Magnitude from Rarefaction and Condensation
Al-Isfahani presents the second proof for magnitude based on rarefaction and condensation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how genuine rarefaction and condensation prove that magnitude is an additional attribute distinct from a body's substance.

Core Idea
Change in volume without change in substance proves magnitude exists.

Al-Isfahani now presents a second proof for the existence of magnitude, this time relying on observable physical phenomena. By examining how bodies can expand and contract without gaining or losing matter, he demonstrates that the volume itself must be an accident distinct from the body's unchanging essence. This lesson walks through that argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the precise definitions of rarefaction and condensation.
2
Identify the two phenomena
Identify genuine rarefaction (volume increase without added matter) and genuine condensation (volume decrease without loss of parts).
3
Understand the premise of unchanged substance
Note that the body's substance (jawhar) remains identical throughout the change. This is key.
The author says substantiality is preserved in both states.
4
Follow the logical deduction
Since the changing volume is not the substance itself, it must be an additional attribute. The author argues that if volume were identical to substance, substance would change.
5
Conclude the existence of magnitude
The variable attribute is an existing thing, namely magnitude. From this, surface and line are also established.
This completes the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثاني الجسم يتخلخل تخلخلاً حقيقياً، وهو أن يزداد حجمه من غير انضمام شيء آخر إليه ومن غير أن يقع بين أجزائه خلاء كالماء إذا سخن تسخيناً شديداً ويتكاثف تكاثفاً حقيقياً، أن ينتقص حجمه من غير أن يزول عنه وهو شيء من أجزائه أو يزول خلاء كان فيما بينها وجوهريته أي حقيقته المخصوصة وهويته المعينة باقية محفوظة في الحالين كما سيأتي والمتغير القابل للصغر والكبر زائد على جوهريته المحفوظة الباقية إذ لو كان عينها أو جزءاً لها لتغيرت بتغيره ووجودي ضرورة لما عرفت من أن المتبدل الزائل والمتجدد لا يكون عدماً محضاً فثبت وجود المقدار الجسمي الذي ينتهي بالسطح المنتهي بالخط فتكون كلها موجودة.
The second proof: The body undergoes genuine rarefaction, which is that its volume increases without any other thing joining it and without any void occurring between its parts, like water when heated intensely, and it undergoes genuine condensation, which is that its volume decreases without anything of its parts leaving it or without any void that was between them being eliminated. And its substantiality, i.e., its specific essence and its determinate identity, remains preserved in both states, as will come. And the variable that is susceptible to smallness and greatness is additional to its preserved, remaining substantiality. For if it were identical to it or a part of it, it would change with its change. And its existence is necessary, because, as you know, that which changes and passes away and that which comes anew cannot be pure non-existence. So the existence of bodily magnitude, which ends with a surface that ends with a line, is established, and thus all of them exist.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof for the existence of magnitude (al-miqdar). The proof relies on the phenomena of genuine rarefaction (takhalkhul) and condensation (takathuf). Genuine rarefaction occurs when a body's volume increases without any external matter being added and without any void appearing between its parts, as when water is heated. Genuine condensation is the opposite: volume decreases without any parts being removed and without a pre-existing void being eliminated. The key point is that the body's substance (jawhar) remains the same throughout; what changes is the volume. Therefore, the variable that changes (size) must be an additional attribute distinct from the substance. If it were the substance itself or a part of it, the substance would change with the change in size, but it does not. Thus, the variable is an existing thing, namely magnitude. Since bodily magnitude (al-miqdar al-jismi) is established, it follows that it ends in a surface, which ends in a line, so all three are existent.

Key Terms
تخلخل
تكاثف
جوهرية
المتغير
المقدار الجسمي
سطح
خط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Rarefaction is just spreading of parts; no new attribute needed.
Correction: Genuine rarefaction increases volume without addition, so the volume itself must be a distinct attribute (magnitude).

Checkpoint
What does genuine rarefaction show about magnitude?
A) Magnitude is identical to the body's substance.
B) Magnitude is an accidental attribute distinct from substance.
C) Magnitude does not exist.
D) Rarefaction is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The phenomena of genuine rarefaction and condensation show that volume is an accident distinct from substance, proving the existence of magnitude.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that your body's volume can change while its substance remains the same. How much of your identity and worth do you attach to your physical form—something that fluctuates? If your true self (your substance) is permanent, why do you fear changes in your appearance or health? What would it take for you to anchor your self-worth in what never changes?
?
The passage emphasizes that genuine change occurs—rarefaction and condensation are real, not just apparent. In your spiritual life, when you repent or strive to improve, is your change genuine, or do you merely rearrange your habits without real transformation? Identify one area where you have rationalized staying the same, and commit today to a genuine, irreversible change in that area.

Answer to the Proof from Rarefaction and Condensation
Al-Isfahani gives the atomist answer to the rarefaction-condensation proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the atomist school responds to the argument from rarefaction and condensation by denying the assumption of genuine rarefaction and exposing its reliance on hylomorphism.

Core Idea
Atomism rejects the need for prime matter by denying genuine rarefaction.

The argument from rarefaction and condensation is often used to support hylomorphism, but atomists have a decisive response. In this passage, al-Isfahani presents the answer: deny that bodies undergo real rarefaction and condensation, and point out that the proof assumes the very position (atomism denial) it seeks to refute. Let's examine the text to see how this refutation works.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without overthinking. Notice the structure: it begins with the answer (wa al-jawab) and then explains the reasoning.
The passage is concise, every word matters.
2
Identify the two parts of the answer
First, al-Isfahani states the answer: deny (man') that the body undergoes real rarefaction/condensation. Second, he explains why: because the proof depends on prime matter and the denial of the indivisible part.
3
Reflect on the logic
Ask yourself: why would denying rarefaction defeat the proof? Because the proof assumes that rarefaction and condensation are real phenomena that require a substrate (prime matter). If an atomist denies the reality of these processes, the proof loses its foundation.
This shows how atomism avoids the need for hylomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب منعه أي منع قبول الجسم للتخلخل والتكاثف الحقيقيين فإنه أيضا فرع وجود الهيولى وقبولها للمقادير المختلفة وإثباتها فرع نفي الذي لا يتجزأ كما ستطلع عليه إن شاء الله تعالى.
And the answer: deny it, i.e., deny that the body is susceptible to genuine rarefaction and condensation. For it is also a branch of the existence of prime matter (hayula) and its reception of different magnitudes, and the proof of that is a branch of the denial of the indivisible part, as you will learn, God willing.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is the answer to the second proof from rarefaction and condensation. The author states that one can simply deny that bodies undergo genuine rarefaction and condensation. The reason is that this proof presumes the existence of prime matter (hayula) that receives different magnitudes, and the proof of prime matter itself depends on denying the indivisible part (al-juz' alladhi la yatajaza). So the whole argument is based on the rejection of atomism. Therefore, for those who accept atomism, the phenomenon of rarefaction is explained differently, and the proof fails.

Key Takeaway
The atomist response to the rarefaction-condensation proof is to deny genuine rarefaction and highlight its dependence on hylomorphism and the denial of atomism.

?
The proof of prime matter relies on denying the indivisible part. In your own spiritual life, are there 'indivisible parts'—core commitments you refuse to question? Are you open to the possibility that your most protected beliefs might be the very thing blocking deeper truth?

First Argument: Time Cannot Be Permanently Subsistent
Al-Isfahani presents the first argument that time cannot have a permanently subsistent essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the mutakallimun's first argument that time cannot have a permanently subsistent essence and why that leads to its denial as a real entity.

Core Idea
If time were permanently subsistent, the flood would be happening today.

The mutakallimun denied time as a real entity, just as they denied number and magnitude. Here, al-Isfahani presents their first argument: if time were a permanently subsistent thing, then all moments would exist together, making past and future events simultaneous. This lesson breaks down that argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage aloud
Read the Arabic text slowly, focusing on its rhythmic structure. Notice the key terms: الزمن, الكم المتصل غير القار, قار الذات.
The passage is short but dense. Take your time.
2
Identify the main claim
The passage states that the mutakallimun denied time for two reasons. The first reason is given here. What is the core logical move?
Look for the conditional: 'if time had a permanently subsistent essence, then...'
3
Analyze the reductio ad absurdum
The argument shows that assuming time is permanently subsistent leads to an absurd conclusion: the flood event would be happening today. Understand why this is impossible.
This is a classic kalam argument: if A, then B; B is false, so A is false.
4
Connect to the broader denial of time
Reflect on why the mutakallimun needed to deny time as a real entity. How does this argument fit into their overall project?
They deny time to preserve the contingency of events and avoid pre-eternal realities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد السابع إنكار المتكلمين للزمن أنهم أعني المتكلمين كما أنكروا العدد والمقدار الذي هو الكم المتصل القار أنكروا أيضاً الزمان الذي هو الكم المتصل غير القار لوجهين. الأول أن الزمان على تقدير كونه موجوداً أمسه مقدم على يومه إذ لا يجوز أن يكون الزمان قار الذات وإلا لكان الحادث في زمان الطوفان حادثاً اليوم وبالعكس وهو باطل
The seventh discourse: The denial of time by the mutakallimun. They, i.e., the mutakallimun, just as they denied number and magnitude which is continuous permanent quantity, they also denied time which is continuous non-permanent quantity, for two reasons. The first: that time, on the assumption of its existence, its yesterday is prior to its day, since it is not permissible for time to have a permanently subsistent essence, for otherwise the event in the time of the flood would be an event today, and vice versa, and that is false.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage introduces the seventh discourse on the denial of time (zaman) by the mutakallimun. The author states that the mutakallimun, having denied number and magnitude (continuous permanent quantity), also deny time (continuous non-permanent quantity). The first argument is as follows: If time were an existing thing, its parts would be ordered such that yesterday is prior to today. This implies that time cannot have a permanently subsistent essence (qar al-dhat). If it were permanently subsistent, all its parts would exist simultaneously. In that case, an event that occurred in the time of the flood would also be occurring today, which is absurd. Therefore, time does not have a permanently subsistent essence. The argument intends to show that time cannot be a real, self-subsistent entity; it must be something else (like a mental construct or relation). The full argument continues with a second reason, but this lesson covers the first.

Key Terms
الزمن
الكم المتصل غير القار
قار الذات
زمان الطوفان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The mutakallimun deny the existence of time altogether.
Correction: The argument only denies that time has a permanently subsistent essence; it does not necessarily deny time's existence as a non-subsistent entity (e.g., a mental construct).

Checkpoint
What absurd consequence follows if time had a permanently subsistent essence according to the first argument?
A) Time would be infinite.
B) Events from different times would occur simultaneously.
C) Time would be divisible.
D) Time would be relative.

Key Takeaway
The mutakallimun's first argument against time shows that if time were a real, permanently subsistent entity, past and present would collapse, proving that time cannot be such an entity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If time is not a permanently subsistent reality, then your past sins are not eternally present. How does this change your motivation to repent and seek forgiveness today?
?
Since yesterday and today cannot coexist, the flood is truly past. What past event in your life—good or bad—are you still carrying as if it were present? What action can you take to release it to Allah?
?
The mutakallimun deny time as a real container. If every moment is directly created by Allah, are you living this moment as if it is a fresh act of His power and mercy? What would change if you truly believed that?

The Argument Against Non-Temporal Priority of Time Parts
Argues that priority of time parts must be temporal, leading to a time for time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the theologians argue that time's parts cannot have non-temporal priority, and how this leads to the impossibility of time's reality.

Core Idea
Time's parts cannot coexist, so any priority between them must be temporal, which is circular.

Theologians denied the reality of time based on the nature of its parts. How can yesterday be prior to today? If the priority is by causality, essence, honor, or rank, the prior and posterior can coexist in existence. But yesterday and today cannot coexist. Therefore, their priority must be temporal, which leads to an infinite regress of times. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem: parts of time cannot coexist
The argument begins by noting that parts of time like yesterday and today cannot exist together. This is the key observation that drives the entire proof.
Think about why yesterday and today cannot be present at the same instant.
2
Learn why temporal priority is the only possibility
The passage examines different types of priority—causal, essential, honorific—and shows they all require coexistence of prior and posterior. Since time parts lack coexistence, their priority cannot be any of these. Only temporal priority remains.
The commentator also addresses objections about the 'prepared' cause and the example of Moses.
3
See the conclusion: time would require another time (regress)
If the priority of time parts is temporal, then time itself has a time, leading to an infinite regress. This is absurd, so the theologians conclude time is not real in the usual sense.
This is a classic argument in Islamic kalam against the independent existence of time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثاني - المقصد السابع : إنكار المتكلمين للزمن بالضرورة، بل يجب أن تكون أجزاؤه ممتنعة الاجتماع، وليس تقدم أمسه على يومه تقدماً بالعلية والذات أي الطبع والشرف والرتبة لأن المتقدم بهذه الوجوه يجامع المتأخر في الوجود وليس الأمس مما يمكن اجتماعه مع اليوم وأيضاً أجزاء الزمان متساوية في الحقيقة فلا يكون احتياج بعضها إلى بعض أولى من عكسه فلا

قوله : ( يجامع المتأخر ) أي يمكن أن يجامع المتأخر نظراً إلى ذاتيهما، وإن امتنع بعارض فلا يرد المعد لأنه من حديث ذاته يمكن اجتماعه إنما امتنع الاجتماع بواسطة عروض التقدم الزماني له بناء على كونه موقوفاً عليه من حيث العدم بعد الوجود .

قوله : ( وليس الأمس إلخ ) فإن أجزاء الزمان في أنفسها يمتنع اجتماعها.

قوله : ( متساوية في الحقيقة ) لأن أجزاء الزمان زمان ولیست موجودة في الخارج فلا يمكن أن يكون احتياج بعضها إلى بعض بحسب التشخص أيضاً، وما قيل : إنّ التشخص الوهمي تتصف به الأجزاء بعد فرض القسمة يجوز أن يصير مرجحاً لاحتياج بعضها إلى بعض فلا يخلو عن مكابرة لأن التشخص الوهمي لا يمكن أن يصير مرجحاً للاحتياج والعلية في الخارج. التقدير يكون حاضراً مجامعاً لليوم الحاضر فما يكون وجوده مقارناً له يكون مقارناً لليوم أيضاً وبالجملة الملازمة بين الشيء وزمانه بيِّن فلا ينفك الحادث عن زمانه وبالعكس، وهذا ظاهر فلا يلتفت إلى ما يتوهم من أنه لا يلزم من دوام الظرف دوام المظروف على أنه إن سلم اجتماع اليوم مع زمان الطوفان وقت حدوث الحادث المذكور فيه فقد اتضح الملازمة، وإن لم يسلم فقد ثبت تقدم ذلك الزمان المعتبر مع عدم اليوم على اليوم بالزمان كتقدم الأب المعتبر من حيث أنه كان مقارناً لعدم الابن عليه فإنه تقدم زماني كما سيجيء. فيلزم أن يكون للزمان زمان وهو المطلوب وبالجملة المنع المذكور وإنما نشأ من عدم تخيل معنى الاجتماع المنافي لتقدم الأمس على اليوم .

قوله : ( لأن المتقدم بهذه الوجوه يجامع المتأخر ) أي يجوز أن يجامعه وإلا فتقدم موسى عليه السلام علينا بالشرف مما لا شك فيه . وقد يمنع لزوم هذا الجواز أيضاً في كل تقدم بالطبع لأن المعد مقدم بالطبع على المعلول، ولا يجوز اجتماعه معه كما هو الصواب والظاهر اجتماع جهتي التقدم في المعد والفرق بالحيثية ولو اعتبر في أحد التقدمين قيد يستلزم عدم اجتماعها الصدق، فليس بضار في التحقيق لأن مجرد عدم جواز اجتماع المقدم مع المؤخر يستدعي الزمان كما يفهم من إطلاقاتهم سواء سمي تقدماً زمانياً أو طبيعياً فيتم المطلوب فتأمل.
The second observation - the seventh aim: The theologians' denial of time necessarily, but rather its parts must be impossible of coexistence, and the priority of its yesterday over its today is not a priority by causality and essence, i.e., nature, and honor and rank, because that which is prior in these respects coexists with the posterior in existence, and yesterday is not such that it can coexist with today. Also, the parts of time are equal in reality, so the dependence of some of them on others is not more appropriate than its opposite, therefore...

His statement: 'coexists with the posterior' means it can coexist with the posterior with respect to their essences, even if it is impossible due to an accident, so the prepared (al-muʿadd) is not an objection because by its essence it can coexist; its non-coexistence is only due to the accidental occurrence of temporal priority upon it based on its being dependent on the other in terms of non-existence after existence.

His statement: 'and yesterday is not etc.' means the parts of time in themselves are impossible to coexist.

His statement: 'equal in reality' because the parts of time are time and do not exist externally, so dependence of some on others cannot be by individuation either. And what is said—that imaginary individuation characterizes the parts after supposing division, and may become a preponderator for dependence of some on others—is not free from obstinacy, because imaginary individuation cannot become a preponderator for dependence and causality externally.

The estimation is present coexisting with the present day, so what has its existence concomitant with it is also concomitant with the day. In short, the concomitance between a thing and its time is evident, so the temporal event is not separate from its time and vice versa. This is apparent, so no attention is paid to the mistaken notion that perpetuity of the container does not necessitate perpetuity of the contained. For if the coexistence of today with the time of the Flood at the time of the occurrence of the mentioned event is granted, then the concomitance is clear; and if not granted, then the priority of that considered time, with the absence of today, over today in time is established, like the priority of the father considered insofar as he was concomitant with the non-existence of the son, for it is temporal priority as will come. Thus it necessarily follows that time has a time, and that is the desired conclusion. In short, the mentioned denial only arose from the lack of imagining the meaning of coexistence that negates the priority of yesterday over today.

His statement: 'because that which is prior in these respects coexists with the posterior' means it is possible for it to coexist with it; otherwise, the priority of Moses, peace be upon him, over us in honor is beyond doubt. And the necessity of this possibility may also be denied in every priority by nature, because the prepared (al-muʿadd) is prior by nature over the effect, and it is not possible for it to coexist with it, as is correct. And the apparent is the coexistence of the two aspects of priority in the prepared, and the distinction is by aspect. Even if in one of the two priorities a condition is considered that necessitates the non-coexistence of their truth, it is not harmful in investigation, because the mere impossibility of the coexistence of the prior with the posterior necessitates time, as understood from their absolute statements, whether it is called temporal priority or natural priority. Thus the desired conclusion is established. So reflect.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage presents a proof that time cannot be real because the parts of time (yesterday and today) cannot coexist, and the only type of priority that does not require coexistence is temporal priority, but that leads to an infinite regress. The author begins by stating that the theologians deny time necessarily. He then argues that the priority of yesterday over today cannot be by causality, essence (nature), honor, or rank, because in all those types the prior and posterior can coexist in existence. Since yesterday and today cannot coexist, those types are impossible. The commentator explains that even if a cause (al-muʿadd) is prior by nature and does not coexist with its effect in some interpretations, the mere impossibility of coexistence requires time, which suffices for the argument. The passage also addresses an objection about the priority of Moses in honor, showing that honor priority allows coexistence, unlike time parts. The conclusion is that the priority must be temporal, meaning time has a time, which is absurd.

الزمان
التقدم
العلية
الذات
الشرف
الرتبة
المعد
التقدم الزماني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that priority by nature (like cause and effect) does not require coexistence, so time parts could have natural priority.
Correction: The argument shows that even natural priority implies coexistence in a certain sense, and if not, it still requires time, leading to the same regress.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that the priority of yesterday over today cannot be by causality, essence, honor, or rank?
A) Because these types of priority require the prior and posterior to coexist, which time parts cannot.
B) Because time is divisible and these types apply only to indivisible entities.
C) Because causality does not apply to temporal relations.
D) Because honor and rank are subjective and not real.

Key Takeaway
Time parts cannot have non-temporal priority, so their priority must be temporal, leading to an infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If time is not a real entity but merely a conceptual relation between events, why do you let the fear of running out of time control your decisions? How would your daily anxieties change if you truly internalized that the 'past' and 'future' cannot even coexist in a single moment?
?
Your attachment to the past (regret) and future (worry) is built on the illusion that time's parts are distinct and real. What one concrete step can you take today to stop treating time as a container for your life and instead focus on the present moment, which alone is real?
?
The argument shows that any priority between time parts requires an infinite regress. This means your perception of time as flowing from past to future is logically flawed. Does this shake your confidence in the way you measure your life—by hours, days, and years? If so, what alternative measure of your life's worth would you adopt?

The Necessity of Temporal Priority for Time Parts
Argues that time parts require temporal priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the necessary priority of yesterday over today can only be temporal priority, given the philosophers' classification of five types of priority.

Core Idea
Yesterday's priority over today is necessary and unchanging; only temporal priority fits.

This passage addresses a subtle objection: even if time parts are equal in reality, equality does not prevent one from being a preparation for another, nor does it block accidental honor. The crucial point is that the priority of yesterday over today is necessary and unchangeable, so it cannot be by rank or honor. Therefore, it must be temporal, leading to the consequence that time itself has a time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on equality and the objection
Read the Arabic passage carefully, focusing on the objection that equality might negate priority. Then read the translation.
Note the phrase 'يمكن أن يقال' which introduces the objection.
2
Understand the response about preparation and honor
The response argues that equality does not prevent one part from being a preparation for another, and priority by honor can be accidental.
3
Identify why priority by rank is excluded
Priority by rank changes with consideration, but the priority of yesterday over today is necessary and unchanging, so it cannot be rank-based.
4
Recognize the five types of priority
The philosophers limit priority to five types: causality, essence, honor, rank, and time. The first four are negated here.
5
Conclude that the priority is temporal
With the other four negated, only temporal priority remains. This implies that time has a time.
This sets up the next lesson on infinite regress.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وأيضاً أجزاء الزمان متساوية في الحقيقة يمكن أن يقال بعد تسليم التساوي في الحقيقة أن التساوي فيها لا ينافي كون السابق معداً للاحق كما في كون إحدى الدورات معدة للأخرى، وعدم الأولوية باعتبار أمر عارض ممنوع على أنه لا يلزم في تقدم الشرف أن يكون المتقدم ذاته منشأ للشرف كما في العالم والجاهل، بل جاز أن يكون باعتبار أمر عارض فكونها
وهي في أنفسها متساوية في الشرف فلا تقدم بحسبه ولا بحسب الرتبة، لأن التقدم الرتبي يتبدل بالاعتبار، وتقدم الأمس على اليوم لازم لا يتبدل ( فهو بالزمان لانحصاره عندكم أيها الحكماء في خمسة فإذا انتفى أربعة منها تعين الخامس ) فيكون للزمان (زمان) لأن معنى التقدم الزماني أن المتقدم في زمان سابق والمتأخر في زمان لاحق فيكون الأمس في زمان متقدم واليوم في زمان متأخر عنه ( والكلام في ذلك الزمان وتقدم بعض أجزائه على بعض ويلزم التسلسل في الأزمنة الموجودة معاً، أي يلزم أن يكون هناك أزمنة غير متناهية منطبق بعضها على بعض ( وأنه محال) في نفسه بالضرورة ومع ذلك أي ومع كونه محالاً يستلزم وهو أن يقال (فمجموع) تلك (الأزمنة) التي لا تتناهى وينطبق بعضها محالاً آخر وهو

قوله: (وهي في أنفسها متساوية إلخ) فلا يعرض لبعضها شرف بالنظر إلى ذاته، وإن اتصف بالشرف بسبب الأمور الواقعة فيه، لأن الكلام في تقدم البعض على البعض.
قوله : (لأن التقدم الرتبي إلخ لأنه لا بد فيه من اعتبار المبدأ وضعاً أو عقلاً وإذا تبدل اعتباره يتبدل التقدم كما في الإمام والمأموم والجنس والنوع .
قوله : ( والكلام في ذلك إلخ) بأن يقال : على تقدير وجوده يكون أمسه مقدماً على يومه إلخ . لا يقال : يجوز أن يكون زمان الزمان اعتبارياً لأنا نقول فيه اعتراف بعدمية الزمان الذي يعرض التقدم والتأخر لأجله والزمان الأول كسائر الزمانيات .
قوله : ( ويلزم التسلسل إلخ بخلاف ما إذا كان عدميا فإنه على تقدير لزوم التسلسل تسلسل في الأمور الاعتبارية .
قوله : (بالضرورة) إذ بداهة العقل تحكم بأن ليس لنا أزمنة غير متناهية منطبقة بعضها على بعض، ذلك يستلزم وجود الحركات الغير المتناهية المستلزم لوجود الأجسام المتحركة الغير المتناهية .
ومع ذلك يستلزم محالاً آخر: قيل : فيه نظر لأن التسلسل محال ولا استحالة في استلزام محال محالاً آخراً وليس بشيء لأن المقصود الاستدلال على عدمية الزمان باستلزام المحال.
His statement: 'And also the parts of time are equal in reality'—it can be said after granting equality in reality that equality therein does not negate the earlier being a preparation for the later, as in the case of one revolution being a preparation for another. And the denial of priority due to an accidental matter is prevented. Moreover, it is not necessary in priority by honor that the prior itself be the source of honor, as in the scholar and the ignorant; rather, it may be due to an accidental matter. So their being...

And they themselves are equal in honor, so there is no priority by it nor by rank, because priority by rank changes with consideration, and the priority of yesterday over today is necessary and does not change. (So it is by time, because it is confined according to you, O philosophers, to five [types]; when four are negated, the fifth is determined.) So time has a time, because the meaning of temporal priority is that the prior is in a previous time and the posterior in a later time. Thus yesterday is in a prior time and today in a later time. (And the discussion is about that time, and the priority of some of its parts over others, and it necessitates an infinite regress in times existing together, i.e., it necessitates that there be infinite times, some of them coinciding with others, and that is impossible in itself necessarily. And along with that, i.e., along with its being impossible, it necessitates another impossibility, namely that the totality of those infinite times, some coinciding with others, is another impossibility.

His statement: 'and they themselves are equal etc.' So honor does not occur to some of them with respect to their essence, even if they are characterized by honor due to events occurring in them, because the discussion is about the priority of some over others.

His statement: 'because priority by rank etc.' because it necessarily involves considering the starting point, either by position or by reason, and when its consideration changes, the priority changes, as in the imam and the follower, and the genus and species.

His statement: 'and the discussion is about that etc.' i.e., it is said: on the assumption of its existence, its yesterday is prior to its today, etc. It should not be said: it is possible that the time of time is mental, because we say in that there is an admission of the non-existence of the time for which priority and posteriority occur, and the first time is like other temporal things.

His statement: 'and it necessitates an infinite regress etc.' contrary to the case if it were non-existent, for then, if regress is necessitated, it would be a regress in mental matters.

His statement: 'necessarily' because the intuition of reason judges that we do not have infinite times coinciding with each other. That necessitates the existence of infinite motions, which necessitates the existence of infinite moving bodies.

And along with that, it necessitates another impossibility. It is said: there is objection because the regress is impossible, and there is no impossibility in an impossibility necessitating another impossibility. And that is nothing, because the purpose is to argue for the non-existence of time by necessitating the impossible.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage continues the argument by addressing a possible objection to the equality of time parts and then shows that the only possible priority is temporal, leading to an infinite regress. The commentator first responds to an objection: even if time parts are equal, equality does not prevent one part from being a preparation for another (like one revolution preparing another). Also, priority by honor does not require the prior to be inherently honorable—it can be accidental. The main text then asserts that time parts are equal in honor and thus cannot have priority by honor or rank (since rank is relative). The priority of yesterday over today is necessary and unchanging, so it must be temporal, because the philosophers limit types of priority to five, and the other four are negated. Therefore, time has a time, meaning yesterday is in a prior time and today in a later time. This leads to an infinite regress of times, each time having a time, all coexisting in a coinciding manner, which is absurd. The commentator explains that priority by rank changes with perspective, unlike temporal priority. He also addresses the objection that the time of time might be mental: admitting it as mental still acknowledges the non-existence of the real time. Finally, he argues that the infinite regress of times is impossible by intuition and leads to other impossibilities like infinite motions and bodies. The passage concludes by refuting a secondary objection that one impossibility implying another is harmless, insisting that the aim is to prove time's non-existence by deriving an impossibility.

التقدم الرتبي
التقدم الزماني
التسلسل

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if time parts are equal in reality, then no part can be prior to another.
Correction: Equality does not negate priority by preparation or accidental honor; also, the necessary and unchanging priority of yesterday over today forces temporal priority.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the priority of yesterday over today not by rank?
A) Because rank changes with consideration.
B) Because yesterday and today are equal in honor.
C) Because temporal priority is the only type that remains.
D) Because the philosophers deny rank.

Key Takeaway
The necessary priority of yesterday over today must be temporal, as other types of priority (causality, essence, honor, rank) are negated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe yesterday is over, but do you truly accept that its priority over today is necessary and unchangeable? How does this reality affect your trust in Allah's Qadr, knowing that the past is fixed and only the present moment is within your control?
?
If priority by rank or honor is not inherent and can shift, why do you often strive for status and recognition from others? How can you instead focus on what truly matters: making the most of the time you have been given?
?
The argument shows that temporal priority is not based on worth but on sheer necessity. In your daily life, do you prioritize tasks based on their true temporal urgency or based on how they make you look? What would change if you aligned your priorities with the reality of time?

The Impossible Infinite Regress of Times
Shows that temporal priority leads to infinite regress, deemed impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the argument for temporal priority leads to an infinite regress of times, which is impossible by intuition and entails further absurdities.

Core Idea
If time has a time, then an infinite number of times must coexist absurdly.

Having established that the priority of yesterday over today is temporal, the argument now examines what that implies: if yesterday is in a prior time and today in a later time, then that prior time itself must have a time, leading to an infinite regress. This is not just a conceptual infinite but an actual infinite of real times, motions, and bodies, which is impossible. The passage then addresses an objection about the mental nature of such times.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on infinite regress
Read the Arabic carefully, noting the structure: statement of regress, explanation, proof of impossibility, objection, answer.
2
Understand how the regress arises
If yesterday is in a prior time and today in a later time, that prior time also has parts that are prior and posterior, leading to an infinite chain.
3
See why the regress is impossible
Intuition (بداهة) judges that there cannot be infinite times all coinciding with each other. This would imply infinite motions and bodies, which are also impossible.
4
Consider the objection and answer
An objector says that one impossibility implying another is harmless, but the reply is that the aim is to prove time's non-existence by deriving any impossibility.
